‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - Weber

‡§∏ ‡§µ‡•à·≥ò ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∏·≥ò‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡••
‡§∏ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ·≥ò ‡§è‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§æ·≥ò‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§•‡§æ·≥ò‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö 1 ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠·≥ò‡§∞‡§§‡§ø ‡§§·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ·≥ò‡§£‡§æ·≥´‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§µ·≥´‡§Ç ‡§∏ ‡§µ‡•à ‡§Ø·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§∞-‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§§·≥ò‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡§É ‡§∏·≥ò‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç
‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. He equips (the MahƒÅvƒ´ra) with its equipments;–inasmuch as he equips it therewith from this and that quarter, that is the equipping nature of the equipments 2 (sambhƒÅra): wheresoever anything of the sacrifice is inherent, therewith he equips it 3.

‡•¶‡•®

‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏-‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§É

‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§ú‡§ø‡§®‡•á ‡§∏·≥ò‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡••
‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•ã ‡§µ‡•à·≥ò ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§ú‡§ø‡§®‡§Ç·≥ò ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û·≥ò ‡§Ω‡§è·≥ò‡§µ‡•à‡§®‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏·≥ò‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§∞‡§§‡§ø ‡§≤‡•ã‡§Æ‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§õ·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ·≥´‡§Å·≥≠‡§∏‡§ø ‡§µ‡•à ‡§≤‡•ã·≥ò‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§É‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•á·≥ò‡§µ‡•à‡§®‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏·≥ò‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§§ ‡§Ω‡§â·≥ò‡§¶‡•Ä‡§ö‡•Ä ‡§π‡§ø·≥ò ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å·≥ò‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø·≥ò‡§ï‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ö‡•Ä·≥ò‡§®‡§ó‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§µ‡•á ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø·≥ò ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡••

‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•ã ‡§µ‡•à·≥ò ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§ú‡§ø‡§®‡§Ç·≥ò ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û·≥ò ‡§Ω‡§è·≥ò‡§µ‡•à‡§®‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏·≥ò‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§∞‡§§‡§ø ‡§≤‡•ã‡§Æ‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§õ·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ·≥´‡§Å·≥≠‡§∏‡§ø ‡§µ‡•à ‡§≤‡•ã·≥ò‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§É‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•á·≥ò‡§µ‡•à‡§®‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏·≥ò‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§§ ‡§Ω‡§â·≥ò‡§¶‡•Ä‡§ö‡•Ä ‡§π‡§ø·≥ò ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å·≥ò‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø·≥ò‡§ï‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ö‡•Ä·≥ò‡§®‡§ó‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§µ‡•á ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø·≥ò ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - Weber

‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§ú‡§ø‡§®·≥´‡§Ç ‡§∏·≥ò‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡••
‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•ã ‡§µ‡•à·≥ò ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§ú‡§ø‡§®‡§Ç·≥ò ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û·≥ò ‡§è‡•ó‡§µ‡•à‡§®‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏·≥ò‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§∞‡§§‡§ø ‡§≤‡•ã‡§Æ‡§§‡§∂‡•ç‡§õ·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§ø ‡§µ‡•à ‡§≤‡•ã·≥ò‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§õ·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§É‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡•ó‡§µ‡•à‡§®‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏·≥ò‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§§ ‡§â·≥ò‡§¶‡•Ä‡§ö‡•Ä ‡§π‡§ø·≥ò ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡•ó‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§ø·≥ò‡§ï‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ö‡•Ä·≥ò‡§®‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§µ‡•á ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø·≥ò ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç
‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. He gets ready a black antelope-skin,–for the black antelope-skin is the sacrifice 4: it is at the

sacrifice he thus prepares (the pot);–with its hairy side (upwards),–for the hairs are the metres: on the metres he thus prepares it;–(spread out) on the left (north) side 5,–for the north is the quarter of men;–on (the skin) with its neck-part to the east 6, for that (tends) towards the gods.

‡•¶‡•©

(‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§≠‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ) ‡§Ö·≥ò‡§≠‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡••
‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ·≥ò‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§Ö·≥ò‡§≠‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡§µ‡•à ‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ·≥ò‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§£‡•à·≥ò‡§µ‡•à‡§®‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏·≥ò‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§®·≥ò‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ß‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø

(‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§≠‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ) ‡§Ö·≥ò‡§≠‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡••
‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ·≥ò‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ω‡§Ö·≥ò‡§≠‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡§µ‡•à ‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ·≥ò‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§£‡•à·≥ò‡§µ‡•à‡§®‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏·≥ò‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§®·≥ò‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - Weber

‡§Ö·≥ò‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡••
‡§µ·≥ò‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ö·≥ò‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§µ‡•à ‡§µ·≥ò‡§ú‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§µ‡•Ä‡•ó‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§£‡•à‡•ó‡§µ‡•à‡§®‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏·≥ò‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç·≥ò ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç
‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. With a spade (he digs out the clay), for the spade is a thunderbolt, and the thunderbolt is vigour: with vigour he thus supplies and completes it (the Pravargya).

‡•¶‡•™

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç
‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. He then takes the lump of clay with the (right) hand and spade on the right (south) side, and with the (left) hand alone on the left (north) side 10, with (VƒÅj. S. XXXVII, 3), ‘O divine Heaven and Earth,’–for when the sacrifice had its head cut off, its sap flowed away, and entered the sky and the earth: what clay (firm matter) there was that is this (earth), and what water there was that is yonder (sky); hence it is of clay and water that the MahƒÅvƒ´ra (vessels) are made: he thus supplies and

completes it (the Pravargya) with that sap; wherefore he says, ‘O divine Heaven and Earth,’–‘May I this day compass for you Makha’s head,’–Makha being the sacrifice, he thus says, ‘May I this day accomplish for you 11 the head of the sacrifice;’–‘on the Earth’s place of divine worship,’–for on a place of divine worship of the earth he prepares it;–‘for Makha thee! for Makha’s head thee!’–Makha being the sacrifice, he thus says, ‘For the sacrifice (I consecrate) thee, for the head of the sacrifice (I consecrate) thee.’

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç
‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. Then an ant-hill 13 (he takes, and puts on the skin), with (VƒÅj. S. XXXVII, 4), ‘Ye divine ants,’–for it was they that produced this: just in accordance with the way in which the head of the sacrifice was there cut off, he now supplies and completes it with those (ants);–’the firstborn of the world,’–the firstborn of the world, doubtless, is this earth 14: it thus is therewith that

he supplies and completes it;–‘may I this day compass for you Makha’s head on the Earth’s place of divine worship:–for Makha thee! for Makha’s head thee!’–the import of this is the same as before.

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç
‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. Then (earth) torn up by a boar (he takes), with (VƒÅj. S. XXXVII, 5), ‘Only thus large was she in the beginning,’–for, indeed, only so large was this earth in the beginning, of the size of a span. A boar, called Em≈´sha, raised her up, and he was her lord PrajƒÅpati: with that mate, his heart’s delight, he thus supplies and completes him 16;–‘may I this day compass for you Makha’s head on the Earth’s place of divine worship: for Makha thee! for Makha’s head thee!’ the import of this is the same as before.

Eggeling
  1. Then ƒÄdƒÅra 18 (-plants), with (VƒÅj. S. XXXVII, 6), ‘Indra’s might ye are,’–for when Indra encompassed him (Vish·πáu) with might, then the vital sap of him, thus encompassed, flowed away; and he lay there stinking, as it were. He said, ‘Verily, after bursting open (ƒÅ-dar), as it were, this vital sap has sung praises:’ thence ƒÄdƒÅra (-plants originated); and because he lay there stinking (p≈´y), as it were, therefore (they are also called) P≈´tƒ´ka; and hence, when placed on the fire

as an offering, they blaze; and hence also they are fragrant, for they originated from the vital sap of the sacrifice. And inasmuch as Indra, on that occasion, encompassed him with might, therefore he says, ‘Indra’s might ye are;’–‘may I this day compass for you Makha’s head on the Earth’s place of divine worship: for Makha thee! for Makha’s head thee!’ the import of this is the same as before.

Eggeling
  1. Then goat’s milk;—for when the sacrifice had its head cut off, its heat went out of it, wherefrom the goat was produced: it is with that heat 19 that he thereby supplies and completes it;–with, ‘For Makha thee! for Makha’s head thee!’ the import of this is the same as before.

Eggeling
  1. These, then, are the five equipments with which he equips (the Pravargya),–fivefold is the sacrifice, and fivefold the victims, and five seasons are in the year, and the year is he that shines yonder, and the Pravargya also is that (sun): it is him he thus gratifies. These (objects), thus brought together, he touches with, ‘For Makha (I consecrate) thee! for Makha’s head thee!’ the import of this is the same as before.

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. Now there is an enclosed space 22 on the north

side: whilst proceeding towards that (shed) they mutter (VƒÅj. S. XXXVII, 7; Rig-v. I, 40, 3), ‘May Brahma·πáaspati go forward!’–Brahma·πáaspati (the lord of devotion) doubtless is he that shines yonder, and the Pravargya also is that one: it is him he thus gratifies; hence he says, ‘May Brahma·πáaspati go forward;’–‘may the goddess Gladness go forward!’–for the goddess Gladness she (VƒÅc 23) is;–‘unto the hero 24, kindly to men and the dispenser of fivefold (offerings),’–he thereby praises and magnifies it (the Pravargya),–‘unto the sacrifice may the gods lead us!’–he thereby makes all the gods its guardians.

Eggeling
  1. It is an enclosed space;–for at that time the gods were afraid, thinking, ‘We hope that the fiends, the Rakshas, will not injure here this our (Pravargya):’ they accordingly enclosed for it this stronghold, and in like manner does this (Sacrificer) now enclose for it this stronghold.

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç
‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. He then deposits (the sambhƒÅras 25) on the mound with, ‘For Makha thee! for Makha’s head thee!’ the import of this is the same as before. He then takes a lump of clay and makes the MahƒÅvƒ´ra (pot) with, ‘For Makha thee! for Makha’s head thee,’–the import of this is

the same as before;–a span high 26, for the head is, as it were, a span high;–contracted in the middle 27, for the head is, as it were, contracted in the middle. At the top he then draws it out (so as to form) a spout 28 of three thumbs‚Äô breadths (high): he thereby makes a nose to this (MahƒÅvƒ´ra, or Pravargya). When it is complete, he touches it with (VƒÅj. S. XXXVII, 8), ‘Makha’s head thou art,’–for it indeed is the head of Makha Saumya (the Soma-sacrifice). In the same way (he makes) the other two (MahƒÅvƒ´ra pots 29); silently two milking-bowls (pinvana 30), and silently two Rauhi·πáa-plates 31.

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç
‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. Verily this sacrifice is PrajƒÅpati, and PrajƒÅpati

is both of this, defined and undefined, limited and unlimited 32. Whatever one does with a Yajus formula, by that one makes up that form of him (PrajƒÅpati) which is defined and limited; and whatever one does silently, by that one makes up that form of him which is undefined and unlimited: verily, then, whosoever, knowing this, does it on this wise, makes up that whole and complete PrajƒÅpati. But he also leaves over a lump of spare (clay) for expiations.

‡§Ö·≥ò‡§• ‡§ó‡§µ‡•á·≥ò‡§ß‡•Å‡§ï‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡§ø‡••
‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§õ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∞·≥ò‡§∏‡•ã ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§§·≥ò‡§§ ‡§è‡§§‡§æ ‡§ì·≥ò‡§∑‡§ß‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§ú‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§ø‡§∞‡•á 33 ‡§§‡•á·≥ò‡§®‡•à‡•ó‡§µ‡•à‡§®‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞·≥ò‡§∏‡•á‡§® ‡§∏·≥ò‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç·≥ò ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§ñ‡§æ·≥ò‡§Ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§ñ·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£ ‡§á·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§æ·≥ò‡§µ‡•á‡§µ ‡§¨·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Å‡§∞‡•á‡§µ‡§Æ‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§∞‡•å ‡§§‡•Ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§™‡§ø·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•á ‡§§‡•Ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§∞‡•å‡§π‡§ø‡§£‡§ï‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡•á‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç
‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. He then smooths 34 it by means of GavedhukƒÅ grass (Coix barbata),–for when the sacrifice had its head cut off, its vital sap flowed away, and therefrom those plants grew up: with that vital sap he thus supplies and completes it;–with, ‘For Makha thee! for Makha’s head thee!’ the import of this is the same as before, In the same way the other two (MahƒÅvƒ´ra pots); silently the two milking-bowls, silently the two Rauhi·πáa-plates.

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. He then fumigates these (vessels) with (VƒÅj. S. XXXVII, 9), ‘With dung of the stallion, the impregnator, I fumigate thee,’–for the

stallion is an impregnator, and the impregnator means vigour: with vigour he thus supplies and completes it,–‘on the Earth’s place of divine worship: for Makha thee, for Makha’s head thee!’ the import of this is the same as before. In the same way (he fumigates) the other two (MahƒÅvƒ´ra pots); silently the two milking-bowls, and silently the two Rauhi·πáa-plates.

(‡§Ω) ‡§Ö·≥ò‡§•‡•à‡§®‡§æ‡§û‡•ç‡§õ‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡••
‡§∂‡•É‡§§·≥´‡§Å·≥≠ ‡§π‡§ø·≥ò ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ·≥ò‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø·≥ò‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ï‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§É ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§æ ‡§µ‡§æ·≥ò ‡§Ω‡§è‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ‡§§ ‡§Ø·≥ò‡§•‡§æ‡§Ø‡§•‡•à‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∞‡•ã·≥ò ‡§Ω‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§ ‡§§‡§æ·≥ò‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•á·≥ò‡§µ‡•à‡§®‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏·≥ò‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§®·≥ò‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡•Å ‡§Ø‡•á·≥ò‡§®‡•à‡§µ ‡§∏‡•Å·≥ò‡§∂‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á·≥ò‡§® ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§Ø‡•á‡§¶·≥ò‡§• ‡§™·≥ò‡§ö‡§®‡§Æ‡§µ‡§ß‡§æ·≥ò‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡§Æ·≥ò‡§µ‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§ñ‡§æ·≥ò‡§Ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§ñ·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£ ‡§Ω‡§á·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§æ·≥ò‡§µ‡•á‡§µ ‡§¨·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Å‡§∞‡•á‡§µ‡§Æ‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§∞‡•å ‡§§‡•Ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§ø·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•á ‡§§‡•Ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä·≥ò·≥´‡§Å·≥ò ‡§∞‡•å‡§π‡§ø‡§£‡§ï‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡•á ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø·≥ò‡§µ‡•à·≥ò‡§µ‡•ã‡§™‡§µ·≥ò‡§™‡•á‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡•ã·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡•á‡§¶·≥ò‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø·≥ò ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ·≥ò‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ß‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø

(‡§Ω) ‡§Ö·≥ò‡§•‡•à‡§®‡§æ‡§û‡•ç‡§õ‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡••
‡§∂‡•É‡§§·≥´‡§Å·≥≠ ‡§π‡§ø·≥ò ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ·≥ò‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø·≥ò‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ï‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§É ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§æ ‡§µ‡§æ·≥ò ‡§Ω‡§è‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•ç‡§µ‡§§ ‡§Ø·≥ò‡§•‡§æ‡§Ø‡§•‡•à‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∞‡•ã·≥ò ‡§Ω‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§ ‡§§‡§æ·≥ò‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•á·≥ò‡§µ‡•à‡§®‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏·≥ò‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§®·≥ò‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡•Å ‡§Ø‡•á·≥ò‡§®‡•à‡§µ ‡§∏‡•Å·≥ò‡§∂‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á·≥ò‡§® ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§Ø‡•á‡§¶·≥ò‡§• ‡§™·≥ò‡§ö‡§®‡§Æ‡§µ‡§ß‡§æ·≥ò‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡§Æ·≥ò‡§µ‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§ñ‡§æ·≥ò‡§Ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§ñ·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£ ‡§Ω‡§á·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§æ·≥ò‡§µ‡•á‡§µ ‡§¨·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Å‡§∞‡•á‡§µ‡§Æ‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§∞‡•å ‡§§‡•Ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§ø·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•á ‡§§‡•Ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä·≥ò·≥´‡§Å·≥ò ‡§∞‡•å‡§π‡§ø‡§£‡§ï‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡•á ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø·≥ò‡§µ‡•à·≥ò‡§µ‡•ã‡§™‡§µ·≥ò‡§™‡•á‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡•ã·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡•á‡§¶·≥ò‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø·≥ò ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ·≥ò‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - Weber

‡§Ö·≥ò‡§•‡•à‡§®‡§æ‡§û‡•ç‡§õ‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø·≥ò 35 ‡••
‡§∂‡•É‡§§·≥´‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø·≥ò ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ·≥ò‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø·≥ò‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§É ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§ ‡§µ‡§æ·≥ò ‡§è‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§ ‡§Ø·≥ò‡§•‡§æ-‡§Ø‡§•‡•à‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∞‡•ã·≥ò‡§Ω‡§õ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§ ‡§§‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•á‡•ó‡§µ‡•à‡§®‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏·≥ò‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç·≥ò ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡•Å ‡§Ø‡•á·≥ò‡§®‡•à‡§µ ‡§∏‡•Å·≥ò‡§∂‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á·≥ò‡§® ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§Ø‡•á‡§¶·≥ò‡§• ‡§™·≥ò‡§ö‡§®‡§Æ‡§µ‡§ß‡§æ·≥ò‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡§Æ·≥ò‡§µ‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§ñ‡§æ·≥ò‡§Ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§ñ·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£ ‡§á·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§æ·≥ò‡§µ‡•á‡§µ ‡§¨·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Å‡§∞‡•á‡§µ‡§Æ‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§∞‡•å ‡§§‡•Ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§™‡§ø·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•á ‡§§‡•Ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§∞‡•å‡§π‡§ø‡§£‡§ï‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡•á ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø·≥ò‡§µ‡•à‡•ó‡§µ‡•ã‡§™‡§µ·≥ò‡§™‡•á‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡•ã·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡•á‡§¶·≥ò‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø·≥ò ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ·≥ò‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç
‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. He then bakes them, for what is baked belongs to the gods. He bakes them by means of bricks, for they it was that did so on that occasion 36: just in accordance with the way in which the head of the sacrifice was there cut off, he now supplies and completes it with those (bricks), But, indeed, let him bake them with anything 37 whereby they may become properly baked. Having laid down the fuel for baking 38, he puts down the MahƒÅvƒ´ra (pot), with, ‘For Makha thee, for Makha’s head thee!’ the import of this is the same as before. In the same way the other two MahƒÅvƒ´ra (pots); silently the two milking-bowls, silently the two Rauhi·πáa-plates. By day he should bury them (in the hole), and by day he should take them out, for the day belongs to the gods.

‡•®‡•®

‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏-‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§É

(·≥´‡§Å·≥≠) ‡§∏ ‡§Ω‡§â·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡••
(‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•É) ‡§ã‡§ú·≥ò‡§µ‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•å ‡§µ‡•à·≥ò ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï·≥ò ‡§Ω‡§ã‡§ú‡•Å‡§É·≥ò ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò·≥´‡§Å·≥ò ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•É‡§ú‡•Å‡§É·≥ò ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§Æ‡•á‡§∑ ‡§Ø·≥ò ‡§Ω‡§è‡§∑ ‡§§·≥ò‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑·≥ò ‡§Ω‡§â ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§•‡§Æ‡§É·≥ò ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡•á‡§§·≥ò‡§Æ‡•á·≥ò‡§µ‡•à‡§§·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú·≥ò‡§µ‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡§ø‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ß‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø

(·≥´‡§Å·≥≠) ‡§∏ ‡§Ω‡§â·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡••
(‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•É) ‡§ã‡§ú·≥ò‡§µ‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•å ‡§µ‡•à·≥ò ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï·≥ò ‡§Ω‡§ã‡§ú‡•Å‡§É·≥ò ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò·≥´‡§Å·≥ò ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•É‡§ú‡•Å‡§É·≥ò ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§Æ‡•á‡§∑ ‡§Ø·≥ò ‡§Ω‡§è‡§∑ ‡§§·≥ò‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑·≥ò ‡§Ω‡§â ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§•‡§Æ‡§É·≥ò ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡•á‡§§·≥ò‡§Æ‡•á·≥ò‡§µ‡•à‡§§·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú·≥ò‡§µ‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡§ø‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - Weber

‡§∏ ‡§â·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡••
‡§ã‡§ú·≥ò‡§µ‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•å ‡§µ‡•à·≥ò ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï·≥ò ‡§ã‡§ú‡•Å‡§É·≥ò ‡§∏‡•ó‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø·≥´‡§Ç ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•É‡§ú‡•Å‡§É·≥ò ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§Æ‡•á‡§∑ ‡§Ø·≥ò ‡§è‡§∑ ‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑·≥ò ‡§â ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§•‡§Æ‡§É·≥ò ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡•á‡§§·≥ò‡§Æ‡•á‡•ó‡§µ‡•à‡§§·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú·≥ò‡§µ‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡§ø‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç
‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. He takes out (the first pot) with (VƒÅj. S. XXXVII, 10), ‘For the righteous one (I take) thee,’–the righteous one, doubtless, is yonder world, for the righteous one means truth; and he that shines yonder is the truth, and the first Pravargya is that (god): it is him he thus gratifies, and therefore he says, ‘For the righteous one (I take) thee.’

‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏-‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§É

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ß‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø

(‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø) ‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡§µ‡•à·≥ò ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•Å·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™·≥ò‡§µ‡§§ ‡§Ω‡§è‡§∑ ‡§π‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Å·≥ò‡§≤‡•ç‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§æ·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§ø·≥ò‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ã ‡§Ω‡§®‡•Å‡§™·≥ò‡§µ‡§§ ‡§Ω‡§è‡§∑·≥ò ‡§Ω‡§â ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•Ä·≥ò‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡•á‡§§·≥ò‡§Æ‡•á·≥ò‡§µ‡•à‡§§·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§π ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß·≥ò‡§µ‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡§ø‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - Weber

‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß·≥ò‡§µ‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡§ø‡••
‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§µ‡•à·≥ò ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•Å‡•ó‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§™·≥ò‡§µ‡§§ ‡§è‡§∑ ‡§π‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç·≥ò‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§æ·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§ø‡•ó‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•Å‡§™·≥ò‡§µ‡§§ 39 ‡§è‡§∑·≥ò ‡§â ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•Ä·≥ò‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡•á‡§§·≥ò‡§Æ‡•á‡•ó‡§µ‡•à‡§§·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§π ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß·≥ò‡§µ‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡§ø‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç
‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. With, ‘For the efficient one thee’ (he takes out the second pot),–the efficient one (sƒÅdhu), doubtless, is he (VƒÅyu, the wind) that purifies here by blowing, for as a permanent one (siddha) he blows through these worlds; and the second Pravargya is that (god): it is him he thus gratifies, and therefore he says, ‘For the efficient one (I take) thee.’

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - Weber

‡§∏‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡••
‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§µ‡•à·≥ò ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§É·≥ò ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§ø·≥ò‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§π‡§ø·≥ò ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á ‡§∏·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ·≥ò‡§®‡§ø ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø·≥ò‡§•‡•ã ‡§Ö‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•à·≥ò ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§ø·≥ò‡§∞‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡•ó‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡•ó‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Ç·≥ò‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á 40 ‡§∏·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ·≥ò‡§®‡§ø ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§Ø·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑·≥ò ‡§â ‡§§‡•É‡§§‡•Ä·≥ò‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ·≥ò‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§·≥ò‡§¶‡•á‡§§·≥ò‡§Æ‡•á‡•ó‡§µ‡•à‡§§·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§§·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§π ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á·≥ò‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡•Ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§™‡§ø·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•á ‡§§‡•Ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ç·≥ò ‡§∞‡•å‡§π‡§ø‡§£‡§ï‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡•á‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç
‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. With, ‘For a good abode thee!’ (he takes out the third pot),–the good abode, doubtless, is this (terrestrial) world, for it is in this world that all creatures abide; and the good abode also is Agni (fire), for Agni abides with all creatures 41 in this world; and the third Pravargya is that (god): it is him he thus gratifies, and therefore he says, ‘For a good abode thee.’ Silently (he takes out) the two milking-bowls, and silently the two Rauhi·πáa-plates.

‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏-‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§É

(‡§Ω) ‡§Ö·≥ò‡§•‡•à‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡§æ·≥ò‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•É‡§£‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡••
(‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø) ‡§Ö‡§ú‡§æ·≥ò‡§Ø‡•à ‡§™·≥ò‡§Ø‡§∏‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§ñ‡§æ·≥ò‡§Ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§ñ·≥ò‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£ ‡§Ω‡§á·≥ò‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§æ·≥ò‡§µ‡•á‡§µ ‡§¨·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Å‡§∞‡•á‡§µ‡§Æ‡§ø·≥ò‡§§‡§∞‡•å ‡§§‡•Ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§ø·≥ò‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•á ‡§§‡•Ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä·≥ò·≥´‡§Å·≥ò ‡§∞‡•å‡§π‡§ø‡§£‡§ï‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡•á‡••

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ß‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø

‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç - Weber

‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§É

‚Ä¶

Eggeling
  1. He then pours goat’s milk upon them 42 (the

first) with, ‘For Makha thee! for Makha’s head thee!’ the import of this is the same as before. In the same way the other two; silently the two milking-bowls, and silently the two Rauhi·πáa-plates.

Eggeling
  1. And, verily, whosoever either teaches, or partakes of, this (Pravargya) enters that life, and that light: the observance of the rule thereof is the same as at the creation 44.

  3. 447:2 Pravargya being masculine, the original would, of course, have ‘him’ here and throughout, the ceremony (just like the sacrifice in general) being indeed looked upon as a person. ↩︎

  6. 448:2 The locative, instead of the accusative, is rather strange here. As it stands, the locative is evidently parallel to ‘yaj√±e’ and ‘chanda·∏•su,’ and one has therefore to supply–he collects (prepares) the Pravargya, viz. by putting the lump of clay and the other objects thereon. ↩︎

  11. 450:1 The pronouns in this and the subsequent corresponding formulas (vƒÅ·πÅ, va·∏•, te) are taken by Mahƒ´dhara as accusatives (’te’ according to him standing for ’tvƒÅm’) to which he supplies ‘ƒÅdƒÅya’–‘having taken you, may I this day compass Makha’s head.’ The pronouns are certainly somewhat awkward, as they can scarcely be taken as genitives of material–of you, of thee. ↩︎

  14. 450:3 Whilst in the text of the formula this word must be taken as being plural ‘prathamajƒÅ·∏•,’ the BrƒÅhma·πáa (making use of the Sandhi-form) treats it as if it were singular ‘prathamajƒÅ.’ Mahƒ´dhara also, apparently influenced by the BrƒÅhma·πáa, explains, ’the earth is the firstborn of creatures, and, from their connection with it, ants also are called firstborn.’ ↩︎

  22. 452:2 Viz. a space five cubits square enclosed with mats on all sides, and with a door on the east side, the ground being raised in the middle so as to form a mound covered with sand (cf. III, 1, 2, 2). The object of this enclosed space is to prevent any unauthorised person (such as the Sacrificer’s wife, and people uninstructed in the scriptures) from seeing the manufacturing of the Mahƒ´vƒ´ra (during which the door is kept closed), as well as the completed pot. The place is to the north of the anta·∏•pƒÅtya peg, the black antelope-skin being spread to the south of it (and immediately north of the materials used in making the pot). ↩︎

  23. 453:1 Thus Mahƒ´dhara, on VƒÅj. S. XXXIII, 89. ↩︎

  24. 453:2 ‘Vƒ´ra,’ apparently an allusion to ‘MahƒÅ-vira’ (great hero), the name of the pot used at the Pravargya. ↩︎

  25. 453:3 Viz. as placed on the black antelope-skin which is carried northwards to the enclosed place by the Adhvaryu and his assistants taking hold of it on all sides. ↩︎

  26. 454:1 That is, from bottom to top, a belt (mekhalƒÅ) running round it at the distance of three thumbs’ breadths from the top (Mahƒ´dhara, and comm. on Katy.). This top part above the belt–here simply called ‘mouth,’ whilst in the ƒÄpast. ≈ör. XV, 2, 14 it is called ‘back’ (sƒÅnu)–ends in a hole for pouring the liquid in and out. ↩︎

  27. 454:2 That is, for taking hold of it (mush·π≠igraha·πáayogyam, comm. on Katy.). ↩︎

  28. 454:3 ‘Mukha,’ for which Katy. XXVI, 1, 16 has ‘ƒÅsecana’ explained by the commentator as a hole (garta; comm. on ƒÄ≈õv. GrÃ•hyas. IV, 3 bila), apparently serving as the mouth, or open part of the vessel which seems to be otherwise closed. The edge of the hole would seem to protract sufficiently from the surface to suggest a similarity to the nose. In making the vessel, it seems first to be left solid, the open part which is to hold the milk being then hollowed out by means of a reed from the top hole to the depth of less than the upper half, the remainder remaining solid. Cf. ƒÄ≈õv. ≈ör. XV, 3, 4. ↩︎

  29. 454:4 Only the first of the three pots is, however, actually used; unless it gets broken by accident. ↩︎

  30. 454:5 According to the comm. on Katy. Sr., these vessels are of the form of the (hand-shaped) bowl of an offering-ladle (sruc, cf. part i, p. 67, note 2). ↩︎

  31. 454:6 The Rauhi·πáa-kapƒÅlas are two round, flat dishes for baking the Rauhi·πáa cakes on. ↩︎

  32. 455:1 Cf. J. Muir, Orig. Sansk. Texts, vol. v, p. 393, where a passage is quoted from Prof. Cowell’s translation of the Maitri-Upanishad (VI, 3), ‘There are two forms of Brahma, the embodied (m≈´rta) and the unembodied (am≈´rta): the former is unreal (asatya), the latter real (satya).’–Cf. Sat. Br. VI, 5, 3, 7. ↩︎

  34. 455:2 The S≈´tras use the verbs ‘≈õlaksh·πáayati, ≈õlaksh·πáƒ´kurvanti’ (to make smooth, or soft), and this, I think, must indeed be the meaning of ‘hinv.’ It would also suit very well the passage III, 5, 1, 35, where it is said that the Vedi is a woman, and that, by sprinkling the former with water, one ‘makes her smooth’ for the gods. The polishing of the vessels is done by rubbing them with GavedhukƒÅ grass, whether with the spike, stem, or leaves is not specified. ↩︎

  42. 457:2 As the pots are, however, standing with their open parts upwards, on sand north of the hole in which they were baked, it would chiefly be inside that they would receive the milk, being thereby cooled (cf.
